                     <div class="listing__space" data-reactid="375">
                      The Bear Den Vacation Home, a uniquely Alaskan log building, provides you an opportunity to experience living in Alaska on a homestead site. This private 2-story home is located on an original Alaskan homestead that has been kept as natural as possible. You will enjoy the mowed yard around the building that has been cut out of the surrounding spruce trees and alders. The property is right in the middle of fantastic Alaskan adventures and scenery. You won't find a nicer or more interesting place to stay!

                     <div class="listing__neighborhood" data-reactid="376">
                      The Bear Den Vacation Home is located in a rural area about one mile north of the community of Anchor Point on the west side of the Alaska Kenai Peninsula. This is a private property with spruce trees, alders and wildflowers providing seclusion for four real-log vacation homes that have raised from local beetle-killed spruce trees. Moose, eagles and other Alaska wildlife are frequently seen on the property. Four active volcanoes can be seen looking across Cook Inlet from Anchor Point and from across the highway near the property. You can enjoy the busy tourist activities in nearby cities such as Kenai and Homer, and then come back to the comfort, quiet and your own personal Alaska home.

This is a private property with spruce trees, alders and wildflowers providing seclusion for four real-log vacation homes that have raised from local beetle-killed spruce trees. Moose, eagles and other Alaska wildlife are frequently seen on the property. Four active volcanoes can be seen looking across Cook Inlet from Anchor Point and from across the highway near the property. You can enjoy the busy tourist activities in nearby cities such as Kenai and Homer, and then come back to the comfort, quiet and your own personal Alaska home.

This is a private property with spruce trees, alders and wildflowers providing seclusion for four real-log vacation homes that have raised from local beetle-killed spruce trees. Moose, eagles and other Alaska wildlife are frequently seen on the property. Four active volcanoes can be seen looking across Cook Inlet from Anchor Point and from across the highway near the property. You can enjoy the busy tourist activities in nearby cities such as Kenai and Homer, and then come back to the comfort, quiet and your own personal Alaska home.

                     <div class="listing__summary" data-reactid="1609">
                      Moose Ridge Lodge is a 3 acre Alaskan homestead built in 1925, overlooking the Kasilof River. The interior has been completely refurbished to include a fully remodeled and stocked kitchen, jacuzzi bathtub, full length windows, all new flooring, paint, etc. The exterior remains the original log structure adding to the uniqueness of this property. The original bunkhouse, cache, green house and outhouse are still located on the property. Long views, wild flowers and frequent wildlife abound.
                     </div>

                      Our cabin has 2 bedrooms, with one queen bed and one double bed. There is a oversized living room with two 8' couches and one 6' couch for plenty of extra sleeping room. The kitchen is fully stocked for all of your meal preparation needs, including loads of small appliances and cookware. Blender, toaster, coffee maker, microwave, Ninja....etc. Games, cards, dice, books and toys are also available in the cabin, as well as current issues of ALASKA magazines. Fresh linens are fully stocked. DVD player and movies are also in the cabin.

                      Quiet and mostly wooded area overlooking the Kasilof River. This property is located on 3 quiet acres.

                      <li data-reactid="1613"><p data-reactid="1614">If you are looking for a vacation rental in the Kenai or (URL HIDDEN) area, stop searching! This is the place! Wish we could give it 6 stars. We spent 4 nights at the cottage from July 30-Aug. 3. We were initially a little nervous about renting a property without any prior reviews, but we saw the owners had very favorable ratings from guests they hosted in their main home. We are extremely glad that we took a chance. Ray and Jyll are honestly the most gracious hosts we have ever worked with, and our family has rented approximately 45-50 vacation properties around the world. They provided excellent communication during the booking process and took time to answer all of our questions about the home and the area prior to arrival. You are not likely to find two nicer people, who really go out of their way to make sure their guests have a very positive experience. Jyll called as we were driving to Kasilof just to make sure we were doing OK. Ray is an experienced outdoorsman, who loves fishing and tells great stories. He taught our two boys (ages 16 and 12) how to fish for salmon in the river by their house. On his day off, he took us down the river on his fishing boat. Our oldest son, who is the fisherman of the family, was in heaven. By the time we left, Ray and Jyll had become great friends, and we were very sad to leave. Moose Ridge Lodge is a fully restored homesteader cabin originally built in the 1920s. Although the exterior of the home looks rustic, Ray has done an excellent job making the interior modern and comfortable, with two bedrooms, a living room with an ample supply of DVDs, and a fully-equipped kitchen. Although there are other homes nearby, the property is quiet and private. There is a nice porch as well as a patio where you can enjoy morning coffee or sit outside for a family meal. The cabin sits at the top of the ridge above the Kasilof River. The owners live nearby at the bottom of the hill, just a short walk away. We were welcomed to their property to fish along the bank of the river, access the internet, and to just hang out on their deck and enjoy nightly conversation around the campfire. The location of Moose Ridge Lodge makes it an excellent base camp for exploring the western Kenai Peninsula. Our family took day trips to Homer (75 min.), (URL HIDDEN) (20 min.), Kenai (20 min.), and Captain Cook (60 min.), but the highlight was always returning home to Moose Ridge Lodge at the end of the day. Although there is still so much of the world left for us to explore, this is one place that we definitely hope to return. </p><span data-reactid="1615">Laura</span><span data-reactid="1616">2016-08-03T00:00:00Z</span></li>
